<p><b>Portuguese people</b> are a <a href="/wiki/Italic_peoples" title="Italic peoples">Romance</a><sup id="cite_ref-Pop_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pop-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Minahan_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minahan-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a> <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">indigenous</a> to <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> that share a common <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Portugal" title="Culture of Portugal">Portuguese culture</a> and speak <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>. Their predominant religion is <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, mainly <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>, though vast segments of the population, especially the younger generations, have no religious affiliation. Historically, the Portuguese people's heritage largely includes the <a href="/wiki/Pre-Celtic" title="Pre-Celtic">pre-Celts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> (<a href="/wiki/Celtiberians" title="Celtiberians">Celtiberians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lusitanians" title="Lusitanians">Lusitanians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gallaecians" class="mw-redirect" title="Gallaecians">Gallaecians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oestriminis" title="Oestriminis">Oestriminis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turduli" title="Turduli">Turduli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Celtici" title="Celtici">Celtici</a>), who became culturally <a href="/wiki/Romanization_(cultural)" title="Romanization (cultural)">Romanized</a> during the conquest of the region by the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Romans" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Romans">ancient Romans</a>. A number of Portuguese also can trace descent from Germanic tribes who arrived after the Roman period as ruling elites, including the <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoths</a> in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Portugal">northern Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Portugal">central Portugal</a>. Finally, also limited converted <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berbers</a> as a result of the Moorish occupation of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a> region of southern Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> conquered the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> during the 2nd and 1st centuries B.C. from the extensive maritime empire of <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">Carthage</a> during the series of <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">Punic Wars</a>.  As a result of <a href="/wiki/Campaign_history_of_the_Roman_military#Conquest_of_the_Iberian_peninsula_(219–18_BC)" title="Campaign history of the Roman military">Roman colonization</a>, the majority of Portuguese language stems from the <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a>. Due to the large historical extent from the 16th century of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Colonization" title="Colonization">colonization</a> of territories in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, as well as historical and recent <a href="/wiki/Emigration" title="Emigration">emigration</a>, Portuguese communities can be found in many diverse regions around the globe, and a large <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_diaspora" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese diaspora">Portuguese diaspora</a> exists.
</p><p>Portuguese people began and led the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Exploration" class="mw-redirect" title="Age of Exploration">Age of Exploration</a> which started in 1415 with the <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_Ceuta" title="Conquest of Ceuta">conquest of Ceuta</a> and culminated in an empire with territories that are now part of over 50 countries. The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> lasted nearly 600 years, seeing its end when <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> was returned to <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Republic of China">China</a> in 1999. The discovery of several lands unknown to the <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europeans</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a> (southwest <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>), helped pave the way for modern <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a> and domination of Western civilization.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry">Ancestry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Ancestry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_origins">Historical origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Historical origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Genetic_history_of_Europe" title="Genetic history of Europe">Genetic history of Europe</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:R1b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="R1b.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/R1b.jpg/220px-R1b.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/R1b.jpg/330px-R1b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/R1b.jpg/440px-R1b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="555" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:R1b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div></div></div></div>
<p>The Portuguese are a Southwestern European population, with origins predominantly from Southern and <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>. The earliest <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">modern humans</a> inhabiting Portugal are believed to have been <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> peoples that may have arrived in the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> as early as 35,000 to 40,000 years ago. Current interpretation of <a href="/wiki/Y-chromosome" class="mw-redirect" title="Y-chromosome">Y-chromosome</a> and <a href="/wiki/MtDNA" class="mw-redirect" title="MtDNA">mtDNA</a> data suggests that modern-day Portuguese trace a significant amount of these lineages to the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">paleolithic</a> peoples who began settling the European continent between the end of the <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_glaciation" title="Wisconsin glaciation">last glaciation</a> around 45,000 years ago.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Y-Haplogroup_R1_distribution.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Y-Haplogroup_R1_distribution.png/220px-Y-Haplogroup_R1_distribution.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Y-Haplogroup_R1_distribution.png/330px-Y-Haplogroup_R1_distribution.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Y-Haplogroup_R1_distribution.png/440px-Y-Haplogroup_R1_distribution.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="333" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Y-Haplogroup_R1_distribution.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Distribution of <a href="/wiki/R1a" class="mw-redirect" title="R1a">R1a</a> (purple) and <b><a href="/wiki/R1b" class="mw-redirect" title="R1b">R1b</a></b> (red). See also <a href="/wiki/File:Haplogroups_europe.png" title="File:Haplogroups europe.png">this map</a> for distribution in Europe.</div></div></div>
<p>Northern Iberia is believed to have been a major Ice-age refuge from which Paleolithic humans later colonized Europe. Migrations from what is now Northern Iberia during the Paleolithic and <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a>, links modern <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberians</a> to the populations of much of <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a> and particularly the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Europe" title="Atlantic Europe">Atlantic Europe</a>. Recent books published by geneticists <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Sykes" title="Bryan Sykes">Bryan Sykes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Oppenheimer" title="Stephen Oppenheimer">Stephen Oppenheimer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spencer_Wells" title="Spencer Wells">Spencer Wells</a> have emphasized the large Paleolithic and Mesolithic Iberian influence in the modern day <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Welsh_people" title="Welsh people">Welsh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_people" title="Scottish people">Scottish</a> gene-pool as well as parts of the <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English</a>. Indeed, Y-chromosome <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup" title="Haplogroup">haplogroup</a> <a href="/wiki/R1b" class="mw-redirect" title="R1b">R1b</a> (of Paleolithic origin) is the most common haplogroup in practically all of the Iberian peninsula and western Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Within the R1b haplogroup there are modal <a href="/wiki/Haplotypes" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplotypes">haplotypes</a>. One of the best-characterized of these haplotypes is the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Modal_Haplotype" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic Modal Haplotype">Atlantic Modal Haplotype</a> (AMH). This haplotype reaches the highest frequencies in the Iberian Peninsula and in the British Isles. In Portugal it reckons generally 65% in the South summing 87% northwards, and in some regions 96%.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> colonization of Europe from <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> beginning around 10,000 years ago reached Iberia, as most of the rest of the continent although, according to the <a href="/wiki/Demic_diffusion" title="Demic diffusion">demic diffusion</a> model, its impact was most in the southern and eastern regions of the European continent.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid15044595_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid15044595-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Starting in the 3rd millennium BC as well as in the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>, the first wave of migrations into Iberia of speakers of <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European languages</a> occurred. These were later (7th and 5th Centuries BC) followed by others that can be identified as <a href="/wiki/Celt" class="mw-redirect" title="Celt">Celts</a>.
</p><p>Urban cultures eventually developed in southeastern Iberia, such as <a href="/wiki/Tartessos" title="Tartessos">Tartessos</a>, influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenician</a> colonization of coastal <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a> Iberia, which later shifted to <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greek</a> colonization. There is very little or no evidence of settlements in <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> by either <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a> or <a href="/wiki/Phoenicians" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenicians">Phoenicians</a> despite some statements to the contrary.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ethnographic_Iberia_200_BCE.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Ethnographic_Iberia_200_BCE.PNG/220px-Ethnographic_Iberia_200_BCE.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Ethnographic_Iberia_200_BCE.PNG/330px-Ethnographic_Iberia_200_BCE.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Ethnographic_Iberia_200_BCE.PNG/440px-Ethnographic_Iberia_200_BCE.PNG 2x" data-file-width="677" data-file-height="630" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ethnographic_Iberia_200_BCE.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ethnographic and Linguistic Map of the Iberian Peninsula at about 200 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>These two processes defined Iberia's, and Portugal's, cultural landscape—Continental in the northwest and Mediterranean towards the southeast, as historian José Mattoso describes it.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
Given the origins from Paleolithic and Neolithic settlers as well as <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-Europeans" title="Proto-Indo-Europeans">Indo-European</a> migrations, one can say that the Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_origin" title="Ethnic origin">ethnic origin</a> is mainly a mixture of pre-Roman, pre-Indo-Europeans (such as, in other parts of Iberia, the <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">Iberians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aquitanian_language" title="Aquitanian language">Aquitanians</a>), and pre-<a href="/wiki/Celtics" class="mw-redirect" title="Celtics">Celtics</a> or para-<a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Lusitanians" title="Lusitanians">Lusitanians</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">Lusitania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> peoples such as <a href="/wiki/Callaici" class="mw-redirect" title="Callaici">Calaicians or Gallaeci</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gallaecia" title="Gallaecia">Gallaecia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Celtici" title="Celtici">Celtici</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cynetes" title="Cynetes">Cynetes</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Alentejo" title="Alentejo">Alentejo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a> were also an important influence on <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Portugal" title="Culture of Portugal">Portuguese culture</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese language</a> derives mostly from <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>.
</p><p>Other minor influences included the <a href="/wiki/Phoenicians" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenicians">Phoenicians</a>/<a href="/wiki/Carthaginians" class="mw-redirect" title="Carthaginians">Carthaginians</a> (small semi-permanent commercial coastal establishments in the south before 200 BC), the <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a> (<a href="/wiki/Silingi" title="Silingi">Silingi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hasdingi" title="Hasdingi">Hasdingi</a>) and the Sarmatian <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alans</a> (both migrated to <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>, while some were partially integrated by the Visigoths and <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoths</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Buri_(Germanic_tribe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Buri (Germanic tribe)">Buri</a>, permanently established in the early 5th century). The <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a> ruled from 711 until the <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a> in 1249. In the 9th and 10th centuries small <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Viking</a><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> raids and settlements also occurred in the North coastal regions of Douro and Minho.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Genetic_history_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="Genetic history of the Iberian Peninsula">Genetic history of the Iberian Peninsula</a></div>
<p>For the <a href="/wiki/Y-chromosome" class="mw-redirect" title="Y-chromosome">Y-chromosome</a> and <a href="/wiki/MtDNA" class="mw-redirect" title="MtDNA">MtDNA</a> lineages of the Portuguese and other peoples see <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20040728005528/http://www.scs.uiuc.edu/~mcdonald/WorldHaplogroupsMaps.pdf">this map</a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060326213734/https://www9.nationalgeographic.com/genographic/atlas.html">this one</a>.
</p><p>Portuguese have also maintained a certain degree of ethnic and cultural specific characteristics-ratio with the <a href="/wiki/Basques" title="Basques">Basques</a>, since ancient times. The results of the present <a href="/wiki/Human_leukocyte_antigen" title="Human leukocyte antigen">HLA</a> study in Portuguese populations show that they have features in common with <a href="/wiki/Basques" title="Basques">Basques</a> and some <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spaniards</a> from <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>: a high frequency of the HLA-<a href="/wiki/Haplotypes" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplotypes">haplotypes</a> A29-B44-DR7 (ancient western Europeans) and A1-B8-DR3 are found as common characteristics.  Many Portuguese, and <a href="/wiki/Basques" title="Basques">Basques</a> do not show the Mediterranean A33-B14-DR1 <a href="/wiki/Haplotype" title="Haplotype">haplotype</a>, confirming a lower admixture with <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean people">Mediterraneans</a>.
The Portuguese have a characteristic unique among world populations: a high frequency of HLA-A25-B18-DR15 and A26-B38-DR13, which may reflect a still detectable founder effect coming from ancient Portuguese, i.e., <a href="/wiki/Oestriminis" title="Oestriminis">Oestriminis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cynetes" title="Cynetes">Cynetes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lusitanians">Lusitanians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Lusitanians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Lusatia" title="Lusatia">Lusatia</a>.</div>
<p>The <b><a href="/wiki/Lusitanians" title="Lusitanians">Lusitanians</a></b> (or <b>Lusitānus/Lusitani</b> in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>) were an <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-Europeans" title="Proto-Indo-Europeans">Indo-European speaking people</a> (likely <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">Celtic</a>) living in the Western <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> long before it became the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> <a href="/wiki/Roman_provinces" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman provinces">province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">Lusitania</a> (modern <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">Extremadura</a> and a small part of <a href="/wiki/Salamanca" title="Salamanca">Salamanca</a>). They spoke the <a href="/wiki/Lusitanian_language" title="Lusitanian language">Lusitanian language</a>, of which only a few short written fragments survive. Most Portuguese consider the Lusitanians as their ancestors. Although the northern regions (Minho, Douro, Tras-os-Montes) identify more with the <a href="/wiki/Gallaecians" class="mw-redirect" title="Gallaecians">Gallaecians</a>.
</p><p>It has been hypothesized that the <a href="/wiki/Lusitanians" title="Lusitanians">Lusitanians</a> may have originated in the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a> and settled in the region in the 6th century BC. Some modern scholars consider them to be indigenous and initially dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Celt" class="mw-redirect" title="Celt">Celts</a>, before gaining full independence from them. The archaeologist <a href="/w/index.php?title=Scarlat_Lambrino&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Scarlat Lambrino (page does not exist)">Scarlat Lambrino</a> proposed that they were originally a tribal  <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> group, related to the <a href="/wiki/Lusones" title="Lusones">Lusones</a>.
</p><p>The first area settled by the <a href="/wiki/Lusitanians" title="Lusitanians">Lusitanians</a> was probably the Douro valley and the region of <a href="/wiki/Beira_Alta_(region)" title="Beira Alta (region)">Beira Alta</a>; then they moved south, and expanded on both sides of the <a href="/wiki/Tagus_river" class="mw-redirect" title="Tagus river">Tagus river</a>, before being conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>.
</p><p>The original Roman province of Lusitania was extended north of the areas occupied by the Lusitanians to include the territories of <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturias</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gallaecia" title="Gallaecia">Gallaecia</a> but these were soon ceded to the jurisdiction of the <i>Provincia Tarraconensis</i> in the north, while the south remained the <i>Provincia Lusitania et <a href="/wiki/Vettones" title="Vettones">Vettones</a></i>. After this, Lusitania's northern border was along the Douro river, while its eastern border passed through <i>Salmantica</i> and <i>Caesarobriga</i> to the <i>Anas</i> (<a href="/wiki/Guadiana" title="Guadiana">Guadiana</a>) river.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Roman_groups">Pre-Roman groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Pre-Roman groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mapa_de_Portugal_tribos_principais.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Mapa_de_Portugal_tribos_principais.png/300px-Mapa_de_Portugal_tribos_principais.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="652" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/41/Mapa_de_Portugal_tribos_principais.png 1.5x" data-file-width="335" data-file-height="728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mapa_de_Portugal_tribos_principais.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing the main pre-Roman tribes in Portugal and their main migrations. <a href="/wiki/Turduli" title="Turduli">Turduli</a> movement in red, <a href="/wiki/Celtici" title="Celtici">Celtici</a> in brown and Lusitanian in a blue colour. Most tribes neighbouring the Lusitanians were dependent on them. Names are in Latin.</div></div></div>
<p>The Lusitanians were a single large <a href="/wiki/Tribe" title="Tribe">tribe</a> that lived between the rivers <a href="/wiki/Douro_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Douro River">Douro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tagus" title="Tagus">Tagus</a>. As the Lusitanians fought fiercely against the Romans for independence, the name Lusitania was adopted by the <a href="/wiki/Gallaeci" title="Gallaeci">Gallaeci</a>, tribes living north of the Douro, and other closely surrounding tribes, eventually spreading as a label to all the nearby peoples fighting Roman rule in the west of Iberia. It was for this reason that the Romans came to name their original province in the area, that initially covered the entire western side of the Iberian peninsula, Lusitania.
</p><p>Tribes, often known by their Latin names, living in the area of modern Portugal, prior to Roman rule:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bardili_(Turduli)" title="Bardili (Turduli)">Bardili (Turduli)</a> <i> – living in the Setúbal peninsula;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bracari" title="Bracari">Bracari</a> <i>– living between the rivers <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A2mega_(river)" title="Tâmega (river)">Tâmega</a> and <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1vado_River" title="Cávado River">Cávado</a>, in the area of the modern city of <a href="/wiki/Braga" title="Braga">Braga</a>;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Callaici" class="mw-redirect" title="Callaici">Callaici</a> <i>– living along and north of the <a href="/wiki/Douro" title="Douro">Douro</a>;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Celtici" title="Celtici">Celtici</a> <i> – Celts living in <a href="/wiki/Alentejo" title="Alentejo">Alentejo</a>;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coelerni" title="Coelerni">Coelerni</a> <i> – living in the mountains between the rivers <a href="/wiki/Tua_River" title="Tua River">Tua</a> and Sabor;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cynetes" title="Cynetes">Cynetes or Conii</a> <i> – living in the <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a> and the south of <a href="/wiki/Alentejo" title="Alentejo">Alentejo</a>;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Equaesi" title="Equaesi">Equaesi</a> <i> – living in the most mountainous region of modern <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grovii" title="Grovii">Grovii</a> <i> – a mysterious tribe living in the Minho valley;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Interamici" title="Interamici">Interamici</a> <i> – living in <a href="/wiki/Tr%C3%A1s-os-Montes_(region)" title="Trás-os-Montes (region)">Trás-os-Montes</a> and in the border areas with <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Province of León">León</a> (in modern <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>);</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leuni" title="Leuni">Leuni</a> <i> – living between the rivers Lima and <a href="/wiki/Minho_(river)" title="Minho (river)">Minho</a>;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Luanqui" title="Luanqui">Luanqui</a> <i> – living between the rivers Tâmega and Tua;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lusitani" class="mw-redirect" title="Lusitani">Lusitani</a> <i> – being the most numerous and dominant of the whole region comprising most of <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Limici" title="Limici">Limici</a> <i> – living in the swamps of the river <a href="/wiki/Limia_(river)" class="mw-redirect" title="Limia (river)">Lima</a>, on the border between Portugal and Galicia);</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Narbasi" title="Narbasi">Narbasi</a> <i> – living in the north of modern Portugal (interior) and nearby area of southern Galicia;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nemetati" title="Nemetati">Nemetati</a> <i> – living north of the Douro Valley in the area of Mondim;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paesuri" title="Paesuri">Paesuri</a> <i> – a dependent tribe of the Lusitanians, living between the rivers Douro and Vouga;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Quaquerni" title="Quaquerni">Quaquerni</a> <i>– living in the mountains at the mouths of rivers Cávado and Tâmega;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Seurbi" title="Seurbi">Seurbi</a> <i> – living between the rivers <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1vado_River" title="Cávado River">Cávado</a> and Lima (or even reaching the river Minho);</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tamagani" title="Tamagani">Tamagani</a> <i> – from the area of <a href="/wiki/Chaves,_Portugal" title="Chaves, Portugal">Chaves</a>, near the river Tâmega;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tapoli" title="Tapoli">Tapoli</a> <i> – another dependent tribe of the Lusitanians, living north of the river Tagus, on the border between modern Portugal and Spain;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Turduli" title="Turduli">Turduli</a> <i> – in the east of <a href="/wiki/Alentejo" title="Alentejo">Alentejo</a> (Guadiana Valley);</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Turduli_Veteres" title="Turduli Veteres">Turduli Veteres</a> <i> – the "ancient Turduli" living south of the estuary of the river Douro;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Turdulorum_Oppida" class="mw-redirect" title="Turdulorum Oppida">Turdulorum Oppida</a> <i> – Turduli living in the Portuguese region of <a href="/wiki/Estremadura_Province_(historical)" title="Estremadura Province (historical)">Estremadura</a>;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Turodi" title="Turodi">Turodi</a> <i> – living in <a href="/wiki/Tr%C3%A1s-os-Montes_(region)" title="Trás-os-Montes (region)">Trás-os-Montes</a> and bordering areas of <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vettones" title="Vettones">Vettones</a> <i> – living in the eastern border areas of Portugal, and in Spanish provinces of <a href="/wiki/%C3%81vila_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ávila (province)">Ávila</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salamanca_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Salamanca (province)">Salamanca</a>, as well as parts of <a href="/wiki/Zamora_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Zamora (province)">Zamora</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toledo_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Toledo (province)">Toledo</a> and <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1ceres_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cáceres (province)">Cáceres</a>;</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zoelae" title="Zoelae">Zoelae</a> <i> – living in the mountains of Serra da Nogueira, Sanabria and Culebra, up to the mountains of <a href="/wiki/Mogadouro" title="Mogadouro">Mogadouro</a> in northern Portugal and adjacent areas of <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>.</i></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Romanization">Romanization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Romanization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="navigation" class="navbox" aria-labelledby="Roman_conquest_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" style="margin:0;float:right;clear:right;width:25.5em;margin-bottom:0.5em;margin-left:1em;;padding:3px"><table class="nowraplinks navbox-vertical mw-collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit"><tbody><tr><th scope="col" class="navbox-title" colspan="2" style="background-color:#C3D6EF;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Campaignbox_Roman_conquest_of_the_Iberian_peninsula" title="Template:Campaignbox Roman conquest of the Iberian peninsula"><abbr title="View this template" style=";background-color:#C3D6EF;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none; padding:0;">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Campaignbox_Roman_conquest_of_the_Iberian_peninsula" title="Template talk:Campaignbox Roman conquest of the Iberian peninsula"><abbr title="Discuss this template" style=";background-color:#C3D6EF;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none; padding:0;">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Campaignbox_Roman_conquest_of_the_Iberian_peninsula&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template" style=";background-color:#C3D6EF;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none; padding:0;">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div><div id="Roman_conquest_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em"><span style="line-height:1.6em"><a href="/wiki/Roman_conquest_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="Roman conquest of the Iberian Peninsula"><span class="wrap">Roman conquest of the Iberian Peninsula</span></a></span></div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="width:100%;padding:0px"><div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Second_Punic_War" title="Second Punic War">Second Punic War</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Celtiberian_Wars" title="Celtiberian Wars">Celtiberian Wars</a> (<a href="/wiki/First_Celtiberian_War" title="First Celtiberian War">First</a>,<a href="/wiki/Celtiberian_Wars#Second_Celtiberian_War" title="Celtiberian Wars">Second</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lusitanian_War" title="Lusitanian War">Lusitanian War</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Numantine_War" title="Numantine War">Numantine War</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sertorian_War" title="Sertorian War">Sertorian War</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_Wars" title="Cantabrian Wars">Cantabrian Wars</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lusitanian_War" title="Lusitanian War">Lusitanian War</a></div>
<p>Since 193 B.C., the Lusitanians had been fighting <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> and its expansion into the peninsula following the defeat and occupation of <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">Carthage</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>. They defended themselves bravely for years, causing the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> invaders serious defeats. In 150 B.C., they were defeated by Praetor <a href="/wiki/Servius_Sulpicius_Galba_(consul_144_BC)" title="Servius Sulpicius Galba (consul 144 BC)">Servius Galba</a>: springing a clever trap, he killed 9,000 Lusitanians and later sold 20,000 more as slaves further northeast in the newly conquered Roman provinces in <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">Gaul</a> (modern <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>) by <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a>.  Three years later (147 B.C.), <a href="/wiki/Viriathus" title="Viriathus">Viriathus</a> became the leader of the Lusitanians and severely damaged the Roman rule in Lusitania and beyond. In 139 B.C. Viriathus was betrayed and killed in his sleep by his companions (who had been sent as emissaries to the Romans), <a href="/wiki/Audax,_Ditalcus_and_Minurus" title="Audax, Ditalcus and Minurus">Audax, Ditalcus and Minurus</a>, bribed by <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Popillius_Laenas" title="Marcus Popillius Laenas">Marcus Popillius Laenas</a>. However, when Audax, Ditalcus and Minurus returned to receive their reward by the Romans, the Consul <a href="/wiki/Quintus_Servilius_Caepio" class="mw-redirect" title="Quintus Servilius Caepio">Servilius Caepio</a> ordered their execution, declaring, "Rome does not pay traitors".
</p><p>After Viriathus' rule, the Lusitanians became largely <a href="/wiki/Romanized" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanized">romanized</a>, adopting Roman culture and the language of <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>. The Lusitanian cities, in a manner similar to those of the rest of the Roman-Iberian peninsula, eventually gained the status of "Citizens of Rome". The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese language</a> itself is a local later evolution of the Roman language, <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> after the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a> in the 5th and 6th centuries.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="General_traits">General traits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: General traits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Procissao_em_Figueiredo_(38).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Procissao_em_Figueiredo_%2838%29.JPG/220px-Procissao_em_Figueiredo_%2838%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Procissao_em_Figueiredo_%2838%29.JPG/330px-Procissao_em_Figueiredo_%2838%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Procissao_em_Figueiredo_%2838%29.JPG/440px-Procissao_em_Figueiredo_%2838%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Procissao_em_Figueiredo_(38).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Procession in <a href="/wiki/Amares_e_Figueiredo" title="Amares e Figueiredo">Amares e Figueiredo</a>, Portugal</div></div></div>
<p>Modern Portuguese are an Iberian ethnic group and share a similar makeup to that of the fellow <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europeans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The Western Coast of Iberia, which composes the land of Galicia and Portugal, was a converging point of migratory movements in the past and during the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese Discoveries</a>. As a result, the Portuguese were introduced to new cultures and ethnicities. With the end of the <a href="/wiki/Assimilado" title="Assimilado">Indigenous Statute</a> in the early 1960s,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> indigenous people of Portuguese colonies were granted Portuguese citizenship as the end of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese colonialism</a> was marked with the hand over of <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> to the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a> in 1999, after 500 years of Portuguese administration. Regarding this, it is comprehensible that any relationship between citizenship and anthropometrical features can be questioned, nevertheless, it is possible to draw the general anthropometrical features of the majority of the Portuguese population. Dark to medium <a href="/wiki/Brown_hair" title="Brown hair">brown hair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brown_eye" class="mw-redirect" title="Brown eye">brown</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hazel_eyes" class="mw-redirect" title="Hazel eyes">hazel</a> eyes are predominant. However, light brown and <a href="/wiki/Blond" title="Blond">blond</a> hair and <a href="/wiki/Blue_eye" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue eye">blue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Green-eyed" class="mw-redirect" title="Green-eyed">green</a> <a href="/wiki/Human_eye" title="Human eye">eyes</a> are also found frequently. <a href="/wiki/Chestnut_hair" class="mw-redirect" title="Chestnut hair">Chestnut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Auburn_hair" title="Auburn hair">auburn-colored hair</a> types occur generally.  Legitimate black hair—not espresso brown—can be found, but it is not very common.  Light, true <a href="/wiki/Red_hair" title="Red hair">red hair</a> (meaning red shades that are non-auburn) is seen on occasion.
</p><p>A recent study by Candille et al. (2012) comparing pigmentation levels between the Portuguese and three other ethnically indigenous European national groups—the Irish, the Polish and the Italians—concluded that, in parts of the body not exposed to the sun, the Irish were in the lightest end of the spectrum, followed by the Portuguese, Poles and Italians, with the latter being darkest. In terms of hair color, the Portuguese averaged lighter hair than Italians and darker than Irish and Poles. The Portuguese exhibited significantly lower frequencies in lighter eye shades in comparison to the Irish and Polish, and marginally less, compared to  Italians.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics_of_Portugal">Demographics of Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Demographics of Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Portugal" title="Demographics of Portugal">Demographics of Portugal</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scientiphicvs_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Scientiphicvs_2010.jpg/220px-Scientiphicvs_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Scientiphicvs_2010.jpg/330px-Scientiphicvs_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Scientiphicvs_2010.jpg/440px-Scientiphicvs_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1728" data-file-height="1152" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scientiphicvs_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portuguese men playing <a href="/wiki/Fado" title="Fado">Fado</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Viana_do_Castelo,_Portugal_(4922364383).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Viana_do_Castelo%2C_Portugal_%284922364383%29.jpg/220px-Viana_do_Castelo%2C_Portugal_%284922364383%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Viana_do_Castelo%2C_Portugal_%284922364383%29.jpg/330px-Viana_do_Castelo%2C_Portugal_%284922364383%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Viana_do_Castelo%2C_Portugal_%284922364383%29.jpg/440px-Viana_do_Castelo%2C_Portugal_%284922364383%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2369" data-file-height="1777" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Viana_do_Castelo,_Portugal_(4922364383).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portuguese women in traditional costumes, from <a href="/wiki/Viana_do_Castelo" title="Viana do Castelo">Viana do Castelo</a></div></div></div>
<p>There are around 10 million native Portuguese in Portugal, out of a total population of 10.34 million (estimate).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Native_minority_languages_in_Portugal">Native minority languages in Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Native minority languages in Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A small minority of about 15,000 speak the <a href="/wiki/Mirandese_language" title="Mirandese language">Mirandese language</a>, (part of the Asturian-Leonese linguistic group which includes the <a href="/wiki/Asturian_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Asturian Language">Asturian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leonese_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Leonese Language">Leonese</a> minority languages of Northwestern Spain <sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>) in the <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">municipalities</a> of <a href="/wiki/Miranda_do_Douro" title="Miranda do Douro">Miranda do Douro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vimioso" title="Vimioso">Vimioso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mogadouro" title="Mogadouro">Mogadouro</a>. All of the speakers are bilingual with <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>.
</p><p>An even smaller minority of no more than 2,000 people speak <a href="/wiki/Barranquenho" title="Barranquenho">Barranquenho</a>, a dialect of Portuguese heavily influenced by <a href="/wiki/Extremaduran_language" title="Extremaduran language">Extremaduran</a>, spoken in the Portuguese town of <a href="/wiki/Barrancos" title="Barrancos">Barrancos</a> (in the border between <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">Extremadura</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, and Portugal).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_minorities_in_Portugal">Ethnic minorities in Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Ethnic minorities in Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some people from the former <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">colonies</a>, namely <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Africa" title="Portuguese Africa">Portuguese Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> (China), <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India" title="Portuguese India">Portuguese India</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a>, have been migrating to Portugal since the 1900s.
</p><p>More recently, a great number of <a href="/wiki/Slavic_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic people">Slavs</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> (now the third biggest <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_minority" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic minority">ethnic minority</a><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>) and <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Moldovans" title="Moldovans">Moldovans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanians</a>, keep migrating to Portugal. There is also a <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Chinese</a> minority, which are mainly of <a href="/wiki/Macanese_people" title="Macanese people">Macau</a> <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_people" title="Cantonese people">Cantonese</a> origin.
</p><p>In addition, there is a small minority of <a href="/wiki/Romani_people#Portugal" title="Romani people">Gypsies</a> (<i>Ciganos</i>) about 40,000 in number,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> about 34,000 in number<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> and an even smaller minority of <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Portugal" title="History of the Jews in Portugal">Jews</a> of about 5,000 people (the majority are <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Sephardi</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Belmonte_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Belmonte Jews">Belmonte Jews</a>, while some are <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Ashkenazi</a>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_diaspora">Portuguese diaspora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Portuguese diaspora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2019-05-06_Empfang_Jorge_Carlos_Fonseca-1190.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/2019-05-06_Empfang_Jorge_Carlos_Fonseca-1190.jpg/180px-2019-05-06_Empfang_Jorge_Carlos_Fonseca-1190.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/2019-05-06_Empfang_Jorge_Carlos_Fonseca-1190.jpg/270px-2019-05-06_Empfang_Jorge_Carlos_Fonseca-1190.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/2019-05-06_Empfang_Jorge_Carlos_Fonseca-1190.jpg/360px-2019-05-06_Empfang_Jorge_Carlos_Fonseca-1190.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2470" data-file-height="3005" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2019-05-06_Empfang_Jorge_Carlos_Fonseca-1190.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verdian</a> President <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Carlos_Fonseca" title="Jorge Carlos Fonseca">Jorge Carlos Fonseca</a></div></div></div>
<p>In the whole world there are easily more than one hundred million people with recognizable Portuguese ancestors, due to the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">colonial expansion</a> and worldwide <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigration</a> of Portuguese from the 16th century onwards to <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Macanese_people" title="Macanese people">Macanese people</a>), <a href="/wiki/East-Timor" class="mw-redirect" title="East-Timor">East-Timor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>. Between 1886 and 1966, Portugal lost to emigration more than any West European country except <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> From the middle of the 19th century to the late 1950s, nearly two million Portuguese left Europe to live mainly in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and with significant numbers to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> About 40 million <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Demography of Brazil">Brazilians</a> have relatively recent Portuguese background, due to massive immigration in the late 19th and early 20th centuries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> About 1.2 million Brazilian citizens are native Portuguese.<sup id="cite_ref-memorialdoimigrante.sp.gov.br_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-memorialdoimigrante.sp.gov.br-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Significant verified Portuguese minorities exist in several countries (see table).<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> In 1989 some 4,000,000 Portuguese were living abroad, mainly in France, Germany, Brazil, the United Kingdom, South Africa, Canada, Venezuela, the United States, the United Arab Emirates.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Within Europe, substantial concentrations of Portuguese may be found in Francophone countries like <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, spurred in part by their linguistic proximity with the French language.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_Sephardi_Jews">Portuguese Sephardi Jews</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Portuguese Sephardi Jews">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Portuguese Sephardi Jews (mostly descendants) are also in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. In Brazil many of the colonists were also originally Sephardi Jews, who, converted, were known as New Christians.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Americas_outside_of_Brazil_and_the_Pacific">The Americas outside of Brazil and the Pacific</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: The Americas outside of Brazil and the Pacific">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3885" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Explorer João Álvares Fagundes commemorative monument surrounded by <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_pavement" title="Portuguese pavement">Portuguese pavement</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_Nova_Scotia" title="Halifax, Nova Scotia">Halifax</a> (up) and <a href="/wiki/Azulejo" title="Azulejo">Azulejos</a>, sign and frame about Portuguese immigration inside a <a href="/wiki/Toronto_subway_and_RT" class="mw-redirect" title="Toronto subway and RT">subway station</a>  in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a> (down) , both in Canada</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, there are Portuguese communities in <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, the <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> states, and <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>. <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Illinois" title="Springfield, Illinois">Springfield, Illinois</a> once possessed the largest Portuguese Community in the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Springfield_Railroads_Improvement_Project_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Springfield_Railroads_Improvement_Project-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> In the Pacific, <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> has a sizable Portuguese element that goes back 150 years (see <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese American">Portuguese Americans</a>), <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> also have Portuguese communities (see <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Australians" title="Portuguese Australians">Portuguese Australians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_New_Zealanders" title="Portuguese New Zealanders">Portuguese New Zealanders</a>).  <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, particularly <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, has developed a significant Portuguese community since 1940 (see <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Canadians" title="Portuguese Canadians">Portuguese Canadians</a>). <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> (See <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Argentine" title="Portuguese Argentine">Portuguese Argentine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_Argentine" title="Cape Verdean Argentine">Cape Verdean Argentine</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Uruguayan" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Uruguayan">Portuguese Uruguayan</a>) had Portuguese immigration in the early 20th century.
Portuguese fishermen, farmers and laborers dispersed across the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> (3.75%<sup id="cite_ref-JoshuaBermuda_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JoshuaBermuda-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> to 10%<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> of the population), <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> (4.3% of the population in 1891),<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Vincent and the Grenadines">St. Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, and the island of <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> where there is high influence from the Portuguese community.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Africans" title="Portuguese Africans">Portuguese Africans</a></div><p>
In the early twentieth century the Portuguese government encouraged white emigration to <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Province_of_Angola" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas Province of Angola">Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Province_of_Mozambique" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas Province of Mozambique">Mozambique</a>, and by the 1970s, there were up to 1 million Portuguese settlers living in their overseas African provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> An estimated 800,000 Portuguese returned to Portugal as the country's African possessions gained independence in 1975, after the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a>, while others moved to <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Santa_Cruz_Bangkok_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Santa_Cruz_Bangkok_2.jpg/210px-Santa_Cruz_Bangkok_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="210" height="307" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Santa_Cruz_Bangkok_2.jpg/315px-Santa_Cruz_Bangkok_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Santa_Cruz_Bangkok_2.jpg/420px-Santa_Cruz_Bangkok_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1176" data-file-height="1719" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Santa_Cruz_Bangkok_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Church,_Bangkok" title="Santa Cruz Church, Bangkok">Santa Cruz Church</a>, Thon Buri District, <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a>, Constructed by Portuguese monks in the 18th Century.</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="In_Europe_outside_of_Portugal">In Europe outside of Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: In Europe outside of Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Luxembourger" title="Portuguese Luxembourger">Portuguese</a> constitute 13% of the population of <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>. In 2006 there were estimates to be around half a million people of Portuguese origin in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Portuguese in the United Kingdom">Portuguese in the United Kingdom</a>)—this is considerably larger than around the 88,000 Portuguese-born people alone residing in the country in 2009 (estimation; however this figure does not include British-born people of Portuguese descent). In areas such as <a href="/wiki/Thetford" title="Thetford">Thetford</a> and the crown dependencies of <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a>, the Portuguese form the largest ethnic minority groups at 30% of the population, 7% and 3% respectively. The British capital <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> is home to the largest number of Portuguese people in the UK, with the majority being found in the boroughs of <a href="/wiki/Royal_Borough_of_Kensington_and_Chelsea" title="Royal Borough of Kensington and Chelsea">Kensington and Chelsea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lambeth" title="Lambeth">Lambeth</a> and <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westminster" title="City of Westminster">Westminster</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The Portuguese diaspora communities still are very attached to their language, their culture and their national dishes and particularly the <a href="/wiki/Bacalhau" title="Bacalhau">bacalhau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_Diaspora_in_the_rest_of_the_world">Portuguese Diaspora in the rest of the world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Portuguese Diaspora in the rest of the world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>There are Portuguese influenced people with their own culture and Portuguese based dialects in parts of the world other than former Portuguese colonies, notably in <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">Curaçao</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Vincent and the Grenadines">St. Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_immigrants_in_Guyana" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese immigrants in Guyana">Portuguese immigrants in Guyana</a>), <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a> and throughout Asia (Main Article <a href="/wiki/Luso-Asians" title="Luso-Asians">Luso-Asians</a>).
</p><p>Luso-Asian communities exist in <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Kristang_people" title="Kristang people">Kristang people</a>), <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Burgher_people" title="Burgher people">Burgher people</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Burghers" title="Portuguese Burghers">Portuguese Burghers</a>), <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Bayingyi_people" title="Bayingyi people">Bayingyi people</a>) <sup id="cite_ref-:0_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_ancestry_in_the_Brazilian_population">Portuguese ancestry in the Brazilian population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Portuguese ancestry in the Brazilian population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section's <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute">factual accuracy</a> may be compromised due to out-of-date information</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2013</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<table class="wikitable" style="margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">
